<div id="review_169182397" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169182397" />
    <a title="Derek" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5420722-derek"><img alt="Derek" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484231855p2/5420722.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/169182397?book_show_action=true">May 18, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Derek" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Derek" href="/user/show/5420722-derek">Derek</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">everyone</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5420722-derek?shelf=sf">sf</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer169182397" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17351859968084191281"><b>This</b> is why I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33918.China_Mi_ville' title='China Miéville' rel='nofollow noopener'>China Miéville</a>!<br/><br/>I recently finished <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68497.The_Scar__New_Crobuzon___2_' title='The Scar (New Crobuzon, #2) by China Miéville' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Scar</a> and was thoroughly disappointed, giving it the lowest rating I've given to one of his books. So, I felt I just had to jump into <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9265453.Embassytown' title='Embassytown by China Miéville' rel='nofollow noopener'>Embassytown</a>, and loved it from the start.<br/><br/>SF is full of "aliens", but for the most part they're odd-looking humans, or at least "people". They're not really all that alien. Miéville's Ariekei are not only completely alien, he never even really clearly describes their appearance - it just isn't that important.</span>
  <span id="freeText17351859968084191281" style="display:none"><b>This</b> is why I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/33918.China_Mi_ville" title="China Miéville" rel="nofollow noopener">China Miéville</a>!<br /><br />I recently finished <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/68497.The_Scar__New_Crobuzon___2_" title="The Scar (New Crobuzon, #2) by China Miéville" rel="nofollow noopener">The Scar</a> and was thoroughly disappointed, giving it the lowest rating I've given to one of his books. So, I felt I just had to jump into <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9265453.Embassytown" title="Embassytown by China Miéville" rel="nofollow noopener">Embassytown</a>, and loved it from the start.<br /><br />SF is full of "aliens", but for the most part they're odd-looking humans, or at least "people". They're not really all that alien. Miéville's Ariekei are not only completely alien, he never even really clearly describes their appearance - it just isn't that important. <br /><br />The Ariekei have a unique form of language - so unique, it's called Language! Each of the Ariekei speaks with two voices simultaneously, and is incapable of even understanding that a single voice can actually <u>be</u> Language. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9265453.Embassytown" title="Embassytown by China Miéville" rel="nofollow noopener">Embassytown</a> delves deeply (and at times almost opaquely) into the meaning of meaning, from semiotics into semantics, and into the difference between simile and metaphor. Along the way, we're asked to take sides on the fall from grace in the Garden of Eden - are we (or the Ariekei) better for the knowledge of Good and Evil, or worse? Miéville's position is clear, and I stand with him. <br /><br />It's not an easy read, especially the later chapters, but it's well worth every ounce of effort you put into it.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17351859968084191281" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2988883694" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2988883694" />
    <a title="Oleksandr Zholud" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4743119-oleksandr-zholud"><img alt="Oleksandr Zholud" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506182069p2/4743119.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2988883694?book_show_action=true">Sep 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Oleksandr Zholud" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Oleksandr Zholud" href="/user/show/4743119-oleksandr-zholud">Oleksandr Zholud</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780345524515" href="/book/show/10838795-embassytown">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2988883694" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9120281964225002106">This is a linguistic SF, which was nominated for both Hugo and Nebula in 2011. It was read as a paret of Author’s birthday challenge in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/474371-hugo-nebula-awards-best-novels?ref=nav_bar_discussions_pane_group' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hugo & Nebula Awards: Best Novels</a> group.<br/><br/>There are quite a few SF works that make languages their main topic, including <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40889.The_Languages_of_Pao' title='The Languages of Pao by Jack Vance' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Languages of Pao</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1199688.Babel_17' title='Babel-17 by Samuel R. Delany' rel='nofollow noopener'>Babel-17</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/285563.Native_Tongue__Native_Tongue___1_' title='Native Tongue (Native Tongue, #1) by Suzette Haden Elgin' rel='nofollow noopener'>Native Tongue</a>. This one is the great addition to the bunch.<br/><br/>The story is set in a distant future on a far-away planet Arieka. The protagonist, a female hyperspace (“immer”) pilot Avice Benner Cho. She grew up in</span>
  <span id="freeText9120281964225002106" style="display:none">This is a linguistic SF, which was nominated for both Hugo and Nebula in 2011. It was read as a paret of Author’s birthday challenge in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/474371-hugo-nebula-awards-best-novels?ref=nav_bar_discussions_pane_group" rel="nofollow noopener">Hugo &amp; Nebula Awards: Best Novels</a> group.<br /><br />There are quite a few SF works that make languages their main topic, including <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/40889.The_Languages_of_Pao" title="The Languages of Pao by Jack Vance" rel="nofollow noopener">The Languages of Pao</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/1199688.Babel_17" title="Babel-17 by Samuel R. Delany" rel="nofollow noopener">Babel-17</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/285563.Native_Tongue__Native_Tongue___1_" title="Native Tongue (Native Tongue, #1) by Suzette Haden Elgin" rel="nofollow noopener">Native Tongue</a>. This one is the great addition to the bunch.<br /><br />The story is set in a distant future on a far-away planet Arieka. The protagonist, a female hyperspace (“immer”) pilot Avice Benner Cho. She grew up in Embassytown, a place for human to live and meet with planet’s inhabitants, Ariekei or Hosts. The natives have a unique language, which is the basis of the novel: it is unique both in representation (a Host has two ‘mouths’ that speak simultaneously) and essence (it can represent only true statements). Coming of humans, who can lie changes everything, even if the author doesn’t follow the easy way of cunning men vs noble locals, but does a much more interesting story. While Hosts are limited to their planet, they have a exclusive biotech, moreover, the book’s setting is largely in that biotech environment – living building, living vehicles, even living breathing/filtering masks.<br /><br />While the language (or more precisely Language) is the basis of the plot, there are some political intrigue, some empire-colony political struggles, a bit of adventure and so on – the book is a great mix that clearly shows Author’s mastery.<br /><br />While not a hard SF per se, it is a great ‘what if’ story with a great consistent world. Recommended<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9120281964225002106" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1520065564" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1520065564" />
    <a title="Maxwell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell"><img alt="Maxwell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1539318702p2/1381728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1520065564?book_show_action=true">Jan 21, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maxwell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maxwell" href="/user/show/1381728-maxwell">Maxwell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audiobook 9780307913814" href="/book/show/16636896-embassytown">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1381728-maxwell?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1520065564" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18104254040742695164"><b>3.5 stars</b><br/><br/>This was my 2nd experience with China Mieville, and just like the first--I read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1506114456?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>The City & the City</a> earlier this year--it was an unparalleled reading experience. One thing I commend Mieville for is his incredibly inventive mind. His ability to create worlds, characters, histories, storylines and all the elements required to develop such complex novels is really astounding. <br/><br/>In <i>Embassytown</i> we follow Avice [forgive me for any spelling errors in this review, I listened to the audiobook and </span>
  <span id="freeText18104254040742695164" style="display:none"><b>3.5 stars</b><br /><br />This was my 2nd experience with China Mieville, and just like the first--I read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1506114456?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">The City &amp; the City</a> earlier this year--it was an unparalleled reading experience. One thing I commend Mieville for is his incredibly inventive mind. His ability to create worlds, characters, histories, storylines and all the elements required to develop such complex novels is really astounding. <br /><br />In <i>Embassytown</i> we follow Avice [forgive me for any spelling errors in this review, I listened to the audiobook and he uses some <b>really</b> weird words], a woman who is returning to her home city as an adult. We get some back story about how she was mythologized in the native alien population, called "ariekei," through the development of their language. The civilians of Embassytown speak with these ariekei, also known as 'hosts,' through the Ambassadors who are born &amp; bred to speak the native's language. I'll stop there because it's complex and you'll find it all out as you read the book. <br /><br />At the center of the story, then, is of course the ideas, concepts and even theology of language. Again what I appreciate about Mieville is that he doesn't sacrifice good narrative and creative settings to deliver a thought-provoking story. He blends both together to create something wholly original. <br /><br />And while the plot overall was sometimes hard to follow--it took me a solid hour of the 12 hours in the audiobook to orient myself to the culture, language and unfolding events--I was never bored. Avice is a great protagonist. And I thought Mieville paced the story perfectly, doling out vital information at just the right moments. My only qualm with the novel was that, like I mentioned, it does take a while to orient yourself in the story at the start. That could be a result of listening to the audiobook as opposed to reading &amp; seeing all the strange words and events on a page. Nevertheless, I was pretty impressed with this one and already plan on diving into more Mieville, hopefully sometime soon.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18104254040742695164" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_617520144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/617520144" />
    <a title="Stuart" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart"><img alt="Stuart" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1452041473p2/9456990.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/617520144?book_show_action=true">May 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stuart" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stuart" href="/user/show/9456990-stuart">Stuart</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=fantastic-weird">fantastic-weird</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=alien-contact">alien-contact</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=literature">literature</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9456990-stuart?shelf=distant-worlds">distant-worlds</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer617520144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer487380851000364762">Embassytown is the god-drug EzRa and I am a helpless Ariekei in thrall to it. China Mieville is a master dealer of an irresistible drug-cocktail depicting alien languages and consciousnesses, galactic politicking, revolutions, personal involvement and loyalty, and a unique world filled with wonder and mystery.<br/><br/>I was pretty cautious to read Embassytown after loving Perdido Street Station, admiring The Scar from a distance, and not getting past the halfway-point of Iron Council. None of his books a</span>
  <span id="freeText487380851000364762" style="display:none">Embassytown is the god-drug EzRa and I am a helpless Ariekei in thrall to it. China Mieville is a master dealer of an irresistible drug-cocktail depicting alien languages and consciousnesses, galactic politicking, revolutions, personal involvement and loyalty, and a unique world filled with wonder and mystery.<br /><br />I was pretty cautious to read Embassytown after loving Perdido Street Station, admiring The Scar from a distance, and not getting past the halfway-point of Iron Council. None of his books are the same, which works in both good ways and bad.<br /><br />Well, it only took the first couple pages to know this book is a winner. With deft and minimal brush strokes he establishes an alien environment worthy of the term "alien", and proceeds to introduce a species that speaks a unique Language that can only express literal truth.<br /><br />Many others have written far more eloquent reviews of the story (particularly Nataliya, Arielle, and Ben Babcock), so I won't go into details, but suffice to say this book blew me away and reminded my why I love science fiction so much. The sense of wonder and originality here was in full force, in a genre where almost every idea would seem to have been done to death already. And yet there were innumerable moments that recalled The Left Hand of Darkness, Dune, Solaris, and the Miyazaki animated film Nausicaä during the climatic final assault by the Absurd).<br /><br />It's a no-brainer that a story whose central plot revolves about language will quickly engage the imagination of readers if done right, and as the son of a linguist who has heard much about grammar and syntax growing up without understanding it fully, I was thrilled to see a book where similes and metaphors where driving forces in the narrative.<br /><br />In short, this book has restored my faith in the ability of sufficiently-skilled storytellers to pen original works that really take readers for a ride. Thank you, I extend both my fanwings and giftwings in gratitude!</span>
  <a data-text-id="487380851000364762" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2448113664" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2448113664" />
    <a title="Anthony" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony"><img alt="Anthony" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534088626p2/4009947.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2448113664?book_show_action=true">Dec 27, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anthony" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anthony" href="/user/show/4009947-anthony">Anthony</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/19755140-embassytown">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=sf-group-2018">sf-group-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=hugo-nominees">hugo-nominees</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=arthur-c-clarke-award-nominees">arthur-c-clarke-award-nominees</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=sf">sf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=locus-award-winners">locus-award-winners</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4009947-anthony?shelf=nebula-nominees">nebula-nominees</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2448113664" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10958272171043096949">I have great respect for China Miéville and his incredibly inventive imagination, and his fierce commitment to exploring complex and provocative aspects of what it means to be alive and sentient. I was very impressed by The City & the City and I was totally blown away by Perdido Street Station. I struggled a great deal with this novel, however. I love its ideas of language and how language shapes our reality and vice versa, and I appreciate his efforts to interrogate colonialism in this novel. B</span>
  <span id="freeText10958272171043096949" style="display:none">I have great respect for China Miéville and his incredibly inventive imagination, and his fierce commitment to exploring complex and provocative aspects of what it means to be alive and sentient. I was very impressed by The City &amp; the City and I was totally blown away by Perdido Street Station. I struggled a great deal with this novel, however. I love its ideas of language and how language shapes our reality and vice versa, and I appreciate his efforts to interrogate colonialism in this novel. But I almost never, until right near the end, felt connected to the characters in this novel in a way that would have allowed me a way in to experiencing the depths of this story in a way that transcended intellectual stimulation. <br /><br />I will wholeheartedly and eagerly seek out more of his ambitious work, and hope that it reaches my heart as well as my mind. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10958272171043096949" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nnE7F0kqIr/fIteWywNPxoA6urht3UtMcl27tJ1nE8VYcWwXGT+Fr3IdrvYq0AaYGhv7xPFooeftDroFfoEoIQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('mQn9DHaVRQaAzanIGVXksebAkI0yI+jg+p7uKeM8+ilfCaoMJoDiFi3y0Kj4hq3vfOHR8a6WAktlze+YANrBzQ==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer4571027991314495298">A British "fantastic fiction" writer. He is fond of describing his work as "weird fiction" (after early 20th century pulp and horror writers such as H. P. Lovecraft), and belongs to a loose group of writers sometimes called New Weird who consciously attempt to move fantasy away from commercial, genre clichés of Tolkien epigons. He is also active in left-wing politics as a member of the Socialist W</span>
  <span id="freeText4571027991314495298" style="display:none">A British "fantastic fiction" writer. He is fond of describing his work as "weird fiction" (after early 20th century pulp and horror writers such as H. P. Lovecraft), and belongs to a loose group of writers sometimes called New Weird who consciously attempt to move fantasy away from commercial, genre clichés of Tolkien epigons. He is also active in left-wing politics as a member of the Socialist Workers Party. He has stood for the House of Commons for the Socialist Alliance, and published a book on Marxism and international law.<br /><br /><i>Excerpted from <a href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/China_Mi%C3%A9ville" rel="nofollow noopener">Wikipedia</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="4571027991314495298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>
